22/09/22, 11:53 - Harshita: About VOICE 4 Girls :

Established in 2011, VOICE 4 Girls is an NGO that works with marginalised adolescent girls in India to re-imagine their identities, capabilities, and futures. We conduct activity-based camps where girls acquire critical knowledge, spoken English and life skills while developing confidence and self-efficacy.

VOICE 4 Girls is partnering with Hyderabad Government Day Schools in 4 different mandals to create champions of gender equality as part of Project REWA! As part of the non-residential model, we are looking to hire interns in part-time and full-time capacities. Students will be interning with us from October to January the. They will be awarded a certificate of appreciation from the Telangana government and a stipend of Rs.7000/- after completing the internship. 


*About Project REWA (Non-Residential Camp in Hyderabad):*

Project Rewa combines the best of technological interventions with conventional face-to-face teaching methods to maximise learning and scale to a broader population. Rewa will focus on imparting knowledge to adolescent girls on health, safety, rights, and future planning. With the help of Rewa sessions, adolescents will learn skills that will help them to negotiate for a better future. VOICE 4 Girls is partnering with Hyderabad Government Day Schools in 4 mandals to create champions of gender equality as part of Project REWA! As part of the non-residential model, we are looking to hire interns in part-time and full-time capacities. Students will be interning with us from October to January. After completing the internship, they will be awarded a certificate of appreciation from the Telangana government and a stipend of Rs. 7,000 /-. 


Part-time: With a minimum requirement of 8 hours a week, part-time interns will be teaching a group of students 2 sessions a week for 4 hours per session. Depending on the flexibility, time available for the intern and the area they reside at schools will be allocated to them. 

Full-time: As full-time interns, students will be teaching different batches of students across Hyderabad schools, depending on the time available for the interns and the area they reside in. Applicants who are free for even one-half of the day but bring a passion for teaching are strongly encouraged to apply in the full-time role as well. 

Application for Project Rewa (kindly fill this form:) https://forms.gle/jwoLKqXRgaP6kDyV9

VOICE 4 Girls is partnering with Telangana and Andhra Pradesh Residential Schools to empower adolescent girls to take charge of their futures and break the cycles of inequity. Students will apply for two roles: Camp Counsellor and Field Coordinator. For the same, we are looking for female interns who will work with us for 15 days.

After the attacks of September 11, a company that had its offices at the World Trade Center invited its executives and employees who had for some reason survived the attack to share their experiences.

- The director of a company was late because it was his son's first kindergarten day;

- A woman was delayed because her alarm clock didn't ring in time;

- One was late because he was stuck on the road where there was an accident;

- Another survivor missed the bus;

- Someone threw food on themselves and needed the time to change;

- One had a problem with his car, which did not start;

- Another one returned to answer the phone;

- Another one had a baby!

- Another didn't get a taxi.

- But the story that impressed the most was that of a man who put on a new pair of shoes that morning, and before he got to work he had a blister. He stopped at the pharmacy for a band aid and that's why he's alive today.

07/12/22, 09:22 - Harshita: 1 *.Soft Failure* 
Soft failure is the type of failure that causes the loss in volatile memory of the computer and not in the persistent storage. Here, the information stored in the non-persistent storage like main memory, buffers, caches or registers, is lost. They are also known as system crash. The various types of soft failures are as follows âˆ’

Operating system failure.
Main memory crash.
Transaction failure or abortion.
System generated error like integer overflow or divide-by-zero error.
Failure of supporting software.
Power failure.

 *2.Hard Failure* 

A hard failure is the type of failure that causes loss of data in the persistent or non-volatile storage like disk. Disk failure may cause corruption of data in some disk blocks or failure of the total disk. The causes of a hard failure are âˆ’

Power failure.
Faults in media.
Read-write malfunction.
Corruption of information on the disk.
Read/write head crash of disk.
Recovery from disk failures can be short, if there is a new, formatted, and ready-to-use disk on reserve. Otherwise, duration includes the time it takes to get a purchase order, buy the disk, and prepare it.

 *3.Network Failure* 
Network failures are prevalent in distributed or network databases. These comprises of the errors induced in the database system due to the distributed nature of the data and transferring data over the network. The causes of network failure are as follows âˆ’

Communication link failure.
Network congestion.
Information corruption during transfer.
Site failures.
Network partitioning.

19/01/23, 09:15 - Harshita: 1 bSemantic understanding is important for natural language processing (NLP) because it allows computers to understand the meaning of human language. Without a deep understanding of semantics, NLP systems would be limited to simple tasks such as word matching and pattern recognition, and would not be able to understand the complexities of human language.
19/01/23, 09:15 - Harshita: 1f
Predicate argument structure, also known as valency, is a linguistic concept that describes the way in which the arguments (also known as complements) of a verb or predicate are related to the verb. It refers to the number and type of arguments that a verb or predicate can take, as well as the grammatical roles that these arguments play in a sentence
19/01/23, 09:15 - Harshita: 1g
Discourse processing in natural language processing (NLP) refers to the study of how meaning is constructed and conveyed in text or speech beyond the sentence level. It involves analyzing the way that sentences and paragraphs are connected to each other, and how they contribute to the overall meaning of a text. This includes understanding the relationships between clauses and sentences, as well as the pragmatic and pragmatic functions of language.
19/01/23, 09:15 - Harshita: 1h
Cohesion in NLP refers to the way in which words, phrases, and sentences within a text relate to each other to create a cohesive and coherent whole. This can include the use of pronouns, conjunctions, and other linking words, as well as the repetition of key terms and concepts. Cohesion is important for making text easy to understand and follow, and can help to create a sense of flow and continuity in a text.

15/03/23, 15:07 - Hrithik GNIT: import csv
with open(r'data.csv') as csvFile:
  examples = [tuple(line) for line in csv.reader(csvFile)]
print(examples)
def get_domains(examples):
    d = [set() for i in examples[0]]
    for x in examples:
        for i, xi in enumerate(x):
            d[i].add(xi)
    return [list(sorted(x)) for x in d]
get_domains(examples)
def g_0(n):
    return ('?',)*n
def s_0(n):
    return ('Phi',)*n
def more_general(h1, h2):
    more_general_parts = []
    for x, y in zip(h1, h2):
        mg = x == '?' or (x != 'Phi' and (x == y or y == 'Phi'))
        more_general_parts.append(mg)
    return all(more_general_parts)

def consistent(hypothesis,example):
    return more_general(hypothesis, example)
def min_generalizations(h, x):
    h_new = list(h)
    for i in range(len(h)):
        if not consistent(h[i:i+1],x[i:i+1]):
            if h[i] != 'Phi':
                h_new[i] = '?'
            else:
                h_new[i] = x[i]
    return [tuple(h_new)]

def generalize_S(x, G, S):
    S_prev = list(S)
    for s in S_prev:
        if s not in S:
            continue
        if not consistent(s,x):
            S.remove(s)
            Splus = min_generalizations(s, x)
            S.update([h for h in Splus if any([more_general(g,h) for g in G])])
            S.difference_update([h for h in S if any([more_general(h, h1) for h1 in S if h != h1])])
    return S

def min_specializations(h, domains, x):
    results = []
    for i in range(len(h)):
        if h[i] == '?':
            for val in domains[i]:
                if x[i] != val:
                    h_new = h[:i] + (val,) + h[i+1:]
                    results.append(h_new)
        elif h[i] != 'Phi':
            h_new = h[:i] + ('Phi',) + h[i+1:]
            results.append(h_new)
    return results

def specialize_G(x, domains, G, S):
    G_prev = list(G)
    for g in G_prev:
        if g not in G:
            continue
        if consistent(g,x):
            G.remove(g)
            Gminus = min_specializations(g, domains, x)
            G.update([h for h in Gminus if any([more_general(h, s) for s in S])])
            G.difference_update([h for h in G if any([more_general(g1, h) for g1 in G if h != g1])])
    return G
def candidate_elimination(examples):
    domains = get_domains(examples)[:-1] 
 
    G = set([g_0(len(domains))])
    S = set([s_0(len(domains))])
    i=0
    print('All the hypotheses in General and Specific boundary are:\n')
    print('\n G[{0}]:'.format(i),G)
    print('\n S[{0}]:'.format(i),S)
    for xcx in examples:
        i=i+1
        x, cx = xcx[:-1], xcx[-1] 
        if cx=='Yes': 
            G  = {g for g in G if consistent(g,x)}
            S = generalize_S(x, G, S)
        else: 
            S = {s for s in S if not consistent(s,x)}
            G = specialize_G(x, domains, G, S)
        print('\n G[{0}]:'.format(i),G)
        print('\n S[{0}]:'.format(i),S)
    return
candidate_elimination(examples)

<h1>  About HTML <h1>
<p>HTML stands for HyperText Markup Language. It is used to design web pages using a markup language. HTML is the combination of Hypertext and Markup language. Hypertext defines the link between web pages.<div> A markup language is used to define the text document within the tag which defines the structure of web pages. This language is used to annotate (make notes for the computer) text so that a machine can understand it and manipulate text accordingly. </div>Most markup languages (e.g. HTML) are human-readable.<br> The language uses tags to define what manipulation has to be done on the text. 
</p>
</body>
</html>

18/03/23, 12:25 - Sreesai GNIT: import numpy as np

class CandidateElimination:
    
    def __init__(self, X, Y):
        self.X = X
        self.Y = Y
        self.S = ['?', '?', '?', '?', '?', '?']
        self.G = [['+', '+', '+', '+', '+', '+'], 
                  ['+', '+', '+', '+', '+', '+'],
                  ['+', '+', '+', '+', '+', '+'],
                  ['+', '+', '+', '+', '+', '+'],
                  ['+', '+', '+', '+', '+', '+']]
        
    def is_consistent(self, h, example):
        for i in range(len(h)):
            if h[i] != '?' and h[i] != example[i]:
                return False
        return True
    
    def get_generalized_hypothesis(self, h, example):
        new_h = list(h)
        for i in range(len(new_h)):
            if new_h[i] == '?':
                new_h[i] = example[i]
            elif new_h[i] != example[i]:
                new_h[i] = '?'
        return new_h
    
    def get_specific_hypothesis(self, G, example):
        new_G = []
        for h in G:
            if self.is_consistent(h, example):
                new_G.append(h)
        return new_G
    
    def learn(self):
        for i in range(len(self.X)):
            x = self.X[i]
            y = self.Y[i]
            if y == '1':
                self.S = self.get_generalized_hypothesis(self.S, x)
                self.G = self.get_specific_hypothesis(self.G, x)
            else:
                for j in range(len(self.G)):
                    h = self.G[j]
                    if self.is_consistent(h, x):
                        self.G[j] = self.get_generalized_hypothesis(h, x)
        return self.S, self.G

12/04/23, 14:04 - Mohit GNIT: 3. LEX program to count the number of lines, spaces and tabs.

/* DESCRIPTION/DEFINITION SECTION */
%{
#include<stdio.h>
int lc=0,sc=0,tc=0,ch=0,wc=0;	 // GLOBAL VARIABLES
%}

// RULE SECTION
%%
[\n] { lc++; ch+=yyleng;}
[ \t] { sc++; ch+=yyleng;}
[^\t] { tc++; ch+=yyleng;}
[^\t\n ]+ { wc++; ch+=yyleng;}
%%

int yywrap(){ return 1; }
/*	 After inputting press ctrl+d		 */

// MAIN FUNCTION
int main(){
	printf("Enter the Sentence : ");
	yylex();
	printf("Number of lines : %d\n",lc);
	printf("Number of spaces : %d\n",sc);
	printf("Number of tabs, words, charc : %d , %d , %d\n",tc,wc,ch);
	
	return 0;
}

int yywrap(){}

int main()

    printf("Number of vowels are:  %d\n", vow_count);

12/04/23, 14:26 - Rahul GNIT: #include <stdio.h>

int main() {
    char operator;
    printf("Enter an operator: ");
    scanf("%c", &operator);

    // Check if the entered operator is an arithmetic operator
    if (operator == '+' || operator == '-' || operator == '*' || operator == '/' || operator == '%') {
        printf("The entered operator '%c' is an arithmetic operator.\n", operator);
    }
    // Check if the entered operator is an assignment operator
    else if (operator == '=' || operator == '+=' || operator == '-=' || operator == '*=' || operator == '/=' || operator == '%=') {
        printf("The entered operator '%c' is an assignment operator.\n", operator);
    }
    else {
        printf("The entered operator '%c' is not a valid arithmetic or assignment operator.\n", operator);
    }

    return 0;
}
